  .linkify {
    display: inline;

          --mr-toggled-font-family: Monospace;
        }

        }

Email display settings

<h2>Email display settings</h2>



        

There is a 

setting

<a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a>

 to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.

<p>There is a <a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a> to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.</p>



        

Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.

<p>Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.</p>



        

If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to 

get
        involved

<a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a>

 in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.

<p>If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to <a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a> in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.</p>

This site hosts public issues in public projects

<h2>This site hosts public issues in public projects</h2>



        

Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.

<p>Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>



        

Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.

<p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>

        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,

VULNERABILITY DETAILS



<b class="line"><!---->VULNERABILITY DETAILS<!----></b>



<br>



<br>





I don't know this is a real bug, or it's a normal behavior, or a known sidechannel attack for fencedframes. If it's not a bug, then sorry for the inconvenience.



<span class="line"><!---->I don't know this is a real bug, or it's a normal behavior, or a known sidechannel attack for fencedframes. If it's not a bug, then sorry for the inconvenience.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





I found 3 cases with fencedframe:



<span class="line"><!---->I found 3 cases with fencedframe:<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





1. I can create two way communication channel between the fencedframe and the embedder. (cross site, localhost <=> 127.0.0.1). You can see this on the attached video and the 2 html (embedder and frame).



<span class="line"><!---->1. I can create two way communication channel between the fencedframe and the embedder. (cross site, localhost &lt;=&gt; 127.0.0.1). You can see this on the attached video and the 2 html (embedder and frame).<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





2. I can focus any focusable element (link, input, button) in the fenced frame from the embedder (change the frame.src. Eg. frame.src = frame.src+"#id" will set the focus to #id element)



<span class="line"><!---->2. I can focus any focusable element (link, input, button) in the fenced frame from the embedder (change the frame.src. Eg. frame.src = frame.src+"#id" will set the focus to #id element)<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





3. I can check when an id is exists in the frame or not (with the frame.src+hash and onblur event. The embedder fires onblur when the frame element exists and receive the focus)



<span class="line"><!---->3. I can check when an id is exists in the frame or not (with the frame.src+hash and onblur event. The embedder fires onblur when the frame element exists and receive the focus)<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





The #2 and #3 are known behavior for iframe, but it's a fenced frame.



<span class="line"><!---->The #2 and #3 are known behavior for iframe, but it's a fenced frame.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





VERSION



<b class="line"><!---->VERSION<!----></b>



<br>





Chrome Version: 105.0.5195.125 stable



<span class="line"><!---->Chrome Version: 105.0.5195.125 stable<!----></span>



<br>





Operating System: 5.18.0-14parrot1-amd64 #1 SMP PREEMPT_DYNAMIC Debian 5.18.14-1parrot1 (2022-08-07) x86_64 GNU/Linux



<span class="line"><!---->Operating System: 5.18.0-14parrot1-amd64 #1 SMP PREEMPT_DYNAMIC Debian 5.18.14-1parrot1 (2022-08-07) x86_64 GNU/Linux<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





REPRODUCTION CASE



<b class="line"><!---->REPRODUCTION CASE<!----></b>



<br>



<br>





I attached the embedder.html and the frame.html as POC for #1. In this poc the embedder can send (any valid js) command to the frame, the frame evals that command then returns the result bit by bit to the embedder. 



<span class="line"><!---->I attached the embedder.html and the frame.html as POC for #1. In this poc the embedder can send (any valid js) command to the frame, the frame evals that command then returns the result bit by bit to the embedder. <!----></span>



<br>



<br>





For cross origin testing I used this urls:



<span class="line"><!---->For cross origin testing I used this urls:<!----></span>



<br>





Embedder => 



<span class="line"><!---->Embedder =&gt; <!----></span>





http://127.0.0.1:8000/embedder.html



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="http://127.0.0.1:8000/embedder.html"><!---->http://127.0.0.1:8000/embedder.html<!----></a>



<br>





Frame => 



<span class="line"><!---->Frame =&gt; <!----></span>





http://localhost:8000/frame.html



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="http://localhost:8000/frame.html"><!---->http://localhost:8000/frame.html<!----></a>



<br>



<br>





1. The embedder set the frame.src hash to any value (need to set src twice) (eg to frame.html#aaa)



<span class="line"><!---->1. The embedder set the frame.src hash to any value (need to set src twice) (eg to frame.html#aaa)<!----></span>



<br>





2, The embedder stores the current timestamp



<span class="line"><!---->2, The embedder stores the current timestamp<!----></span>



<br>





3. The frame detects onhashchange, and creates an input and sets it's id to this new hash value (aaa)



<span class="line"><!---->3. The frame detects onhashchange, and creates an input and sets it's id to this new hash value (aaa)<!----></span>



<br>





4. The frame starts a setTimeout(()=>document.location=document.location,millis). This will focus the input after millis time. The data is "encoded" into the length of the time.



<span class="line"><!---->4. The frame starts a setTimeout(()=&gt;document.location=document.location,millis). This will focus the input after millis time. The data is "encoded" into the length of the time.<!----></span>



<br>





5- When the input focused the frame removes the input (onfocus -> removechild)



<span class="line"><!---->5- When the input focused the frame removes the input (onfocus -&gt; removechild)<!----></span>



<br>





6. The embedder receives the onblur event when the input focused in the frame. It's calculates the time beetween the src change and the onblur event. Here is the data, eg. 100-200ms = 0, 200-300 ms = 1, 500ms+ end of data.



<span class="line"><!---->6. The embedder receives the onblur event when the input focused in the frame. It's calculates the time beetween the src change and the onblur event. Here is the data, eg. 100-200ms = 0, 200-300 ms = 1, 500ms+ end of data.<!----></span>



<br>





7. The embedder creates an input with any id (eg. bbb)



<span class="line"><!---->7. The embedder creates an input with any id (eg. bbb)<!----></span>



<br>





8. The embedder calls an child iframe for change the embedder location with the new input id in the hash (embedder.html#bbb) (maybe can done without an iframe, but only this worked for me)



<span class="line"><!---->8. The embedder calls an child iframe for change the embedder location with the new input id in the hash (embedder.html#bbb) (maybe can done without an iframe, but only this worked for me)<!----></span>



<br>





9. The embedder receives the focus from the frame



<span class="line"><!---->9. The embedder receives the focus from the frame<!----></span>



<br>





10. The embedder removes the input



<span class="line"><!---->10. The embedder removes the input<!----></span>



<br>





11. Again from 1 for next bit until all bits are received



<span class="line"><!---->11. Again from 1 for next bit until all bits are received<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





This POC works with fencedframe, but not for iframe. I don't know why it's not working with iframe, but it's only a side note, the fencedframe is the main target.



<span class="line"><!---->This POC works with fencedframe, but not for iframe. I don't know why it's not working with iframe, but it's only a side note, the fencedframe is the main target.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





You can see it in action on the attached video.



<span class="line"><!---->You can see it in action on the attached video.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





2nd and 3rd case:



<span class="line"><!---->2nd and 3rd case:<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





You need just change the fencedframe src to focus any element in the frame. And you can search for any id with the onblur event. This was my original poc, #1 bornt from this.



<span class="line"><!---->You need just change the fencedframe src to focus any element in the frame. And you can search for any id with the onblur event. This was my original poc, #1 bornt from this.<!----></span>



<br>





 



<span class="line"><!----> <!----></span>



<br>





The focus.html shows how to scan a fenced frame for id-s and how to focus an element in the frame from outside (a link in this POC). This file for #2 and #3. I didn't create video for this cases. This is a simple code, I can't give better description than my code.



<span class="line"><!---->The focus.html shows how to scan a fenced frame for id-s and how to focus an element in the frame from outside (a link in this POC). This file for #2 and #3. I didn't create video for this cases. This is a simple code, I can't give better description than my code.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>



<br>





Sorry if something is not clear, this is my first ticket here and english is not my main language, but you can reach me anytime to clarify things.



<span class="line"><!---->Sorry if something is not clear, this is my first ticket here and english is not my main language, but you can reach me anytime to clarify things.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





FOR CRASHES, PLEASE INCLUDE THE FOLLOWING ADDITIONAL INFORMATION



<b class="line"><!---->FOR CRASHES, PLEASE INCLUDE THE FOLLOWING ADDITIONAL INFORMATION<!----></b>

Thanks for filing sokkis@! From running this locally, it seems like the attack in the demo is only possible when fenced frames are enabled with the ShadowDOM architecture via chrome://flags/#enable-fenced-frames, and not "multiple page architecture". Is that right? If these attacks aren't possible with MPArch, then I think that is OK since we're currently not using ShadowDOM architecture in the wild anymore, and are removing it entirely very soon 



<span class="line"><!---->Thanks for filing sokkis@! From running this locally, it seems like the attack in the demo is only possible when fenced frames are enabled with the ShadowDOM architecture via chrome://flags/#enable-fenced-frames, and not "multiple page architecture". Is that right? If these attacks aren't possible with MPArch, then I think that is OK since we're currently not using ShadowDOM architecture in the wild anymore, and are removing it entirely very soon <!----></span>





https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/chromium/src/+/3918971



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/chromium/src/+/3918971"><!---->https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/chromium/src/+/3918971<!----></a>

Same-document navigations through frame.src were disabled in MPArch with this CL, which is in effect from M106 onwards: 



<span class="line"><!---->Same-document navigations through frame.src were disabled in MPArch with this CL, which is in effect from M106 onwards: <!----></span>





https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/chromium/src/+/3785109



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/chromium/src/+/3785109"><!---->https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/chromium/src/+/3785109<!----></a>



<br>



<br>





I believe this explains why Dom was only able to reproduce the issue for ShadowDOM locally (he was probably using Canary, which is M108), vs. M105 here.



<span class="line"><!---->I believe this explains why Dom was only able to reproduce the issue for ShadowDOM locally (he was probably using Canary, which is M108), vs. M105 here.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





In terms of why it works in fenced frames but not iframes, that might be a different in focus behavior; I'll defer to Liam.



<span class="line"><!---->In terms of why it works in fenced frames but not iframes, that might be a different in focus behavior; I'll defer to Liam.<!----></span>

I was able to get your demo to work with iframes. This is on MacOS in both Stable 105.0.5195.125 and Canary 108.0.5330.0.



<span class="line"><!---->I was able to get your demo to work with iframes. This is on MacOS in both Stable 105.0.5195.125 and Canary 108.0.5330.0.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





So it looks like iframes and fenced frames are both happily working with the FragmentAnchor class (I don't think we ever audited the FragmentAnchor path specifically, but I remember discussions in the past on URL restrictions).



<span class="line"><!---->So it looks like iframes and fenced frames are both happily working with the FragmentAnchor class (I don't think we ever audited the FragmentAnchor path specifically, but I remember discussions in the past on URL restrictions).<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





It also looks like this focus pulling can happen with opaque-ads fenced frames as well, and I think this will bypass k-anonymity checks since the navigation is coming from within the frame after it loads. And with this, the embedding page can also pull focus out of a fenced frame without user activation.



<span class="line"><!---->It also looks like this focus pulling can happen with opaque-ads fenced frames as well, and I think this will bypass k-anonymity checks since the navigation is coming from within the frame after it loads. And with this, the embedding page can also pull focus out of a fenced frame without user activation.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Question for the team:



<span class="line"><!---->Question for the team:<!----></span>



<br>





Are there legitimate use cases for URL fragments inside fenced frames? My first thought would be to not allow the `#id` part of a URL to do anything. But I think we're touching upon the larger url restrictions debate at this point.



<span class="line"><!---->Are there legitimate use cases for URL fragments inside fenced frames? My first thought would be to not allow the `#id` part of a URL to do anything. But I think we're touching upon the larger url restrictions debate at this point.<!----></span>

And my last version for today. With this version, I was able to avoid reloading the frame at every data bit.



<span class="line"><!---->And my last version for today. With this version, I was able to avoid reloading the frame at every data bit.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





The problem is that the fencedframe can navigate itself to different hashes, thereby gaining focus, and the embedder can, by definition, do anything, so can obtain the focus anytime. The focus is the key, the frame can obtain the focus programmatically, without interaction.



<span class="line"><!---->The problem is that the fencedframe can navigate itself to different hashes, thereby gaining focus, and the embedder can, by definition, do anything, so can obtain the focus anytime. The focus is the key, the frame can obtain the focus programmatically, without interaction.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Since with this method it is possible to create a protocol in which the master is changed after every request (it's sounds funny, but really, it's a simple 1 wire serial line with fixed baud rate and timing), this reload after every request can also be eliminated, since not only the embedder can receive data with the focus-blur time, but also the frame, they just need to know who is next in line who can ask the other, eg. they can communicate alternately. If I have time on the weekend, I'll do it just for fun. :D



<span class="line"><!---->Since with this method it is possible to create a protocol in which the master is changed after every request (it's sounds funny, but really, it's a simple 1 wire serial line with fixed baud rate and timing), this reload after every request can also be eliminated, since not only the embedder can receive data with the focus-blur time, but also the frame, they just need to know who is next in line who can ask the other, eg. they can communicate alternately. If I have time on the weekend, I'll do it just for fun. :D<!----></span>

I missed my proposal: don't allow the FF to change itself the hash or/and don't change the focus if the hash changed programmatically (with location).



<span class="line"><!---->I missed my proposal: don't allow the FF to change itself the hash or/and don't change the focus if the hash changed programmatically (with location).<!----></span>



<br>





Also as I see, not only the FF can change itself the hash, if I put a child FF into the FF, then also this can change the location and the hash of its parent. The fix in 106, what killed my original poc only prevents the embedder to make change, but not the FF or its children, so its easy to get around, this is why I can do a working poc for the 106 version. 



<span class="line"><!---->Also as I see, not only the FF can change itself the hash, if I put a child FF into the FF, then also this can change the location and the hash of its parent. The fix in 106, what killed my original poc only prevents the embedder to make change, but not the FF or its children, so its easy to get around, this is why I can do a working poc for the 106 version. <!----></span>



<br>





But the good news is that the #2 and #3 cases are resolved, so only the #1, the comminication channel is remaining.



<span class="line"><!---->But the good news is that the #2 and #3 cases are resolved, so only the #1, the comminication channel is remaining.<!----></span>

<span class="line"><!---->  <!----></span>





https://chromium.googlesource.com/chromium/src/+/855a43d7acc395d80c3932d382061ade2c82626e



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://chromium.googlesource.com/chromium/src/+/855a43d7acc395d80c3932d382061ade2c82626e"><!---->https://chromium.googlesource.com/chromium/src/+/855a43d7acc395d80c3932d382061ade2c82626e<!----></a>

<br>





commit 



<span class="line"><!---->commit <!----></span>





855a43d7acc395d80c3932d382061ade2c82626e



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://crrev.com/855a43d7acc395d80c3932d382061ade2c82626e"><!---->855a43d7acc395d80c3932d382061ade2c82626e<!----></a>



<br>





Author: Liam Brady <



<span class="line"><!---->Author: Liam Brady &lt;<!----></span>





lbrady@google.com



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="/u/lbrady@google.com"><!---->lbrady@google.com<!----></a>





>



<span class="line"><!---->&gt;<!----></span>



<br>





Date: Thu Oct 20 21:37:34 2022



<span class="line"><!---->Date: Thu Oct 20 21:37:34 2022<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Fenced frame: have anchor focus require user activation



<span class="line"><!---->Fenced frame: have anchor focus require user activation<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Currently, focus can be pulled across a fenced frame boundary without



<span class="line"><!---->Currently, focus can be pulled across a fenced frame boundary without<!----></span>



<br>





any user activation by using anchor fragments (aka setting location.href



<span class="line"><!---->any user activation by using anchor fragments (aka setting location.href<!----></span>



<br>





to a.com#anchor). We already have script-based focus properly gated, but



<span class="line"><!---->to a.com#anchor). We already have script-based focus properly gated, but<!----></span>



<br>





this is a corner case that we missed.



<span class="line"><!---->this is a corner case that we missed.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





This CL adds a new variable to FocusParams(): `gate_on_user_activation`.



<span class="line"><!---->This CL adds a new variable to FocusParams(): `gate_on_user_activation`.<!----></span>



<br>





If set to true, then focus that crosses a fenced frame boundary will



<span class="line"><!---->If set to true, then focus that crosses a fenced frame boundary will<!----></span>



<br>





only be allowed to happen if the target frame has transient user



<span class="line"><!---->only be allowed to happen if the target frame has transient user<!----></span>



<br>





activation. This check takes place in

Fenced frame: have anchor focus require user activation



<span class="line"><!---->Fenced frame: have anchor focus require user activation<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Currently, focus can be pulled across a fenced frame boundary without



<span class="line"><!---->Currently, focus can be pulled across a fenced frame boundary without<!----></span>



<br>





any user activation by using anchor fragments (aka setting location.href



<span class="line"><!---->any user activation by using anchor fragments (aka setting location.href<!----></span>



<br>





to a.com#anchor). We already have script-based focus properly gated, but



<span class="line"><!---->to a.com#anchor). We already have script-based focus properly gated, but<!----></span>



<br>





this is a corner case that we missed.



<span class="line"><!---->this is a corner case that we missed.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





This CL adds a new variable to FocusParams(): `gate_on_user_activation`.



<span class="line"><!---->This CL adds a new variable to FocusParams(): `gate_on_user_activation`.<!----></span>



<br>





If set to true, then focus that crosses a fenced frame boundary will



<span class="line"><!---->If set to true, then focus that crosses a fenced frame boundary will<!----></span>



<br>





only be allowed to happen if the target frame has transient user



<span class="line"><!---->only be allowed to happen if the target frame has transient user<!----></span>



<br>





activation. This check takes place in



<span class="line"><!---->activation. This check takes place in<!----></span>



<br>





`Frame::AllowFocusWithoutUserActivation()`.



<span class="line"><!---->`Frame::AllowFocusWithoutUserActivation()`.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





This CL also updates the Focus() call in



<span class="line"><!---->This CL also updates the Focus() call in<!----></span>



<br>





`ElementFragmentAnchor::ApplyFocusIfNeeded` to set



<span class="line"><!---->`ElementFragmentAnchor::ApplyFocusIfNeeded` to set<!----></span>



<br>





`gate_on_user_activation` to true. This has the effect of treating



<span class="line"><!---->`gate_on_user_activation` to true. This has the effect of treating<!----></span>



<br>





anchor focusing as a programmatic focus. However, there isn't a



<span class="line"><!---->anchor focusing as a programmatic focus. However, there isn't a<!----></span>



<br>





legitimate use case where a fenced frame will need to pull focus into



<span class="line"><!---->legitimate use case where a fenced frame will need to pull focus into<!----></span>



<br>





itself without user gesture using anchor focusing, and, the behavior



<span class="line"><!---->itself without user gesture using anchor focusing, and, the behavior<!----></span>



<br>





will remain unchanged for anchor focusing that does not cross a fenced



<span class="line"><!---->will remain unchanged for anchor focusing that does not cross a fenced<!----></span>



<br>





frame boundary. So, it's okay to add this restriction.



<span class="line"><!---->frame boundary. So, it's okay to add this restriction.<!----></span>

*** Boilerplate reminders! ***



<span class="line"><!---->*** Boilerplate reminders! ***<!----></span>



<br>





Please do NOT publicly disclose details until a fix has been released to all our users. Early public disclosure may cancel the provisional reward. Also, please be considerate about disclosure when the bug affects a core library that may be used by other products. Please do NOT share this information with third parties who are not directly involved in fixing the bug. Doing so may cancel the provisional reward. Please be honest if you have already disclosed anything publicly or to third parties. Lastly, we understand that some of you are not interested in money. We offer the option to donate your reward to an eligible charity. If you prefer this option, let us know and we will also match your donation - subject to our discretion. Any rewards that are unclaimed after 12 months will be donated to a charity of our choosing.

        /*
         * Really specific class names are necessary because ShadowDOM
         * is disabled for this component.
         */
        .chops-autocomplete-container {
          position: relative;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container table {
          padding: 0;
          font-size: var(--chops-main-font-size);
          color: var(--chops-link-color);
          position: absolute;
          background: var(--chops-white);
          border: var(--chops-accessible-border);
          z-index: 999;
          box-shadow: 2px 3px 8px 0px hsla(0, 0%, 0%, 0.3);
          border-spacing: 0;
          border-collapse: collapse;
          /* In the case when the autocomplete extends the
           * height of the viewport, we want to make sure
           * there's spacing. */
          margin-bottom: 1em;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container tbody {
          display: block;
          min-width: 100px;
          max-height: 500px;
          overflow: auto;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container tr {
          cursor: pointer;
          transition: background 0.2s ease-in-out;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container tr[data-selected] {
          background: var(--chops-active-choice-bg);
          text-decoration: underline;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container td {
          padding: 0.25em 8px;
          white-space: nowrap;
        }
        .screenreader-hidden {
          clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);
          height: 1px;
          overflow: hidden;
          position: absolute;
          white-space: nowrap;
          width: 1px;
        }
